          "text": "'## N01: \"THE\\xa0GRIP\\xa0THAT\\xa0HOLDS\" — MASTER STORY BIBLE\\n\\n**Purpose:** This document contains everything a writer or AI model needs to know to generate prose for the first novella of the Confluence Chronicles. It summarizes the world, characters, relationships, and structural expectations for N01, and it clearly outlines what can and cannot be revealed. Anything not covered here must remain unknown until later books.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### NOVELLA OVERVIEW\\n\\n* **Title:** N01 \"The\\xa0Grip\\xa0That\\xa0Holds\"\\n* **Position:** First novella of six‑Turning structure (Turning\\xa01:\\xa0GLASS)\\n* **Acrostic Letter:** **G** (begins the word GLASS)\\n* **Timeline:** Tide\\xa00 (the Piercing) through Tide\\xa05\\n* **Word Count Target:** 18\\u202f000–21\\u202f000 words\\n* **Chapter Count:** 12 chapters + 2 interludes + 1 epilogue\\n\\n**Core Arc:** N01 tells the story of how Jhace Torrins discovers his Soulpulse ability during the Piercing, how he and Tiffani Merrow learn to trust one another, and how they decide to face the city\\'s crisis together. They navigate guild politics, institutional power plays, and the physical cost of magic. By the end of N01 they have formed a partnership in both work and love, though it remains physically unconsummated due to exhaustion and circumstances.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### WORLD STATE AT THE START OF N01\\n\\n**Pre‑Piercing Baseline:** Saint\\xa0Merro is a terraced city with a functional guild system. Higher districts are wealthier and more stable; lower districts are older and fragile. The technology level is roughly renaissance/proto‑industrial: water and wind mills, simple steam engines, printing presses, and advanced metallurgy. There is no electricity, and the predominant light sources are oil and candles. Communication happens via runners and signal flags. No one has ever seen or done anything like Soulpulse.\\n\\n**The Piercing Event (Tide\\xa00):** A massive cylindrical object enters the atmosphere at an impossible angle and speeds, warping light as it passes. It shears across the sky without touching the ground and continues into space. Shockwaves shatter structures; dust and metallic particles rain down. Many buildings collapse; hundreds die. Traditional physics fails at the quantum level. This is the inciting incident of the entire saga.\\n\\n**Post‑Piercing Conditions:** The city is partially destroyed. Institutions are overwhelmed. Resources are scarce. People are traumatized. New abilities (Soulpulse) begin to emerge in roughly 1 in 500 individuals. The heat‑grid, critical to winter survival, is failing. Guilds fracture over how to respond. The Regulatory and Reconstruction Office (RRO) forms to coordinate relief but quickly drifts toward control and bureaucracy.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### PRIMARY CHARACTERS\\n\\nSee `Character_Dossiers_N01.md` for full psychological profiles, humor styles and arcs. A concise summary follows.\\n\\n#### Jhace Torrins\\n\\n* **Age:** 29 Turns; structural engineer and heat‑grid inspector.\\n* **Backstory:** His parents died in a building collapse when he was 7. Ever since, he has obsessed over preventing preventable deaths. He works alone to avoid sharing his anxiety with others. He refuses apprentices to keep his hypervigilance from infecting someone else.\\n* **Soulpulse:** Instinctively activates during the Piercing. Discovers it requires direct contact and protective desperation. Learns cost (tremor, pain, exhaustion) as he uses it repeatedly. Stage progression goes from baseline to Stage\\xa01 through this novella. He reaches the threshold of Stage\\xa02 by the final chapters.\\n* **Psychology:** Hypervigilant, guilt‑driven, physically oriented. Terse, literal, thinks in terms of weight and vibration. Hates being called a hero. Lies to others (and himself) that he\\'s \"fine.\" Needs to prevent death above all.\\n* **Arc:** Moves from isolated vigilante to co‑lead in a partnership. Learns to trust Tiffani\\'s analytical mind. Accepts help. Admits romantic feelings. Commits to working together \"when the world is broken.\"\\n\\n#### Tiffani Merrow\\n\\n* **Age:** 27 Turns; precision glassworker, atmospheric observer.\\n* **Backstory:** Her friend Marisse died in a glass‑house accident because Tiffani dismissed abnormal temperature readings. She now views pattern recognition as a sacred duty. Precision is her way to save lives.\\n* **Soulpulse:** She cannot use Soulpulse herself but becomes the first and best analyst of its patterns. She logs and categorizes every use, advising Jhace on load paths and stress points.\\n* **Psychology:** Analytical yet deeply caring. Precision is empathy. Humor emerges through sharp wit and occasional sex jokes. She fears missing patterns more than being wrong. She pretends confidence she doesn’t feel because appearing uncertain makes others panic.\\n* **Arc:** Moves from detached observer to invested partner. She teaches Jhace to optimize his technique and reduce cost. She learns that people aren’t structures; human patterns are messier. She goes from refusing to rest to allowing herself to be cared for.\\n\\n#### Bram Kelter\\n\\n* **Age:** 52 Turns; forgemaster and mentor figure.\\n* **Role:** Grounding force, comic relief, voice of experience. He regrets compromising his innovations for guild approval. He sees his younger self in Jhace and doesn’t want him to burn out. He provides wry commentary and practical support.\\n\\n#### Other Supporting Characters\\n\\n* **Chloen:** Teen apprentice who looks up to Jhace. Saved in Ch\\xa03 by his first Soulpulse; leg heals inexplicably.\\n* **Pella:** Tiffani’s apprentice. Brings her food and learns observation. Mirrors Tiffani’s younger self but with healthier patterns.\\n* **Kylar:** Soulpulse trainee. Fails catastrophically on first attempt. Shows that not everyone can handle power, but failure can teach humility.\\n* **Corlexi:** RRO official. Represents systematic order. Begins pressing for registration and control of Soulpulse users. Unknowingly one of four mortal vessels for cosmic forces.\\n* **Salee:** Community organizer. Believes relationships and networks save lives. Establishes mutual aid in the Dregs. Another mortal vessel.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### SOULPULSE MECHANICS IN N01\\n\\nSummarized from `Soulpulse_System_N01_Scope.md`:\\n\\n* **Activation:** Requires skin contact with the material and a desperate need to protect. Casual attempts fail.\\n* **Visual:** Copper‑gold glow spreads from the user’s hands into the material. Vein‑lines appear on their arms.\\n* **Cost:** The more you use, the worse the tremor and pain. Stage\\xa01 emerges after 2–3 uses (minor tremor). By the end of the book Jhace’s tremor never fully fades and faint vein‑lines remain visible; he’s on the cusp of Stage\\xa02.\\n* **Unknowns:** Characters don’t know why Soulpulse exists, what powers it, or the risk of further stages. They have no language for \"Stage\\xa03\" or \"Stage\\xa04.\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n### RELATIONSHIP SUMMARY\\n\\nFor full dynamics by chapter, see `Relationship_Dynamics_N01.md`. Key arcs:\\n\\n* **Jhace & Tiffani:** From mutual misconceptions to professional respect to deep partnership and romantic acknowledgment. They end the book committed to working together and being together but are physically too exhausted for sex.\\n* **Jhace & Bram:** Mentorship and camaraderie. Bram is protective but cannot stop Jhace; he can only slow the burn.\\n* **Tiffani & Pella:** Mentor/student showing healthier pattern recognition habits.\\n* **Jhace & Chloen:** Reluctant hero/hero‑worship, hinting at the next generation.\\n* **J/T & Corlexi:** Brewing political conflict. They resist registration; he sees them as unpredictable variables.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### CHAPTER STRUCTURE AND INTERLUDES\\n\\n* N01 has **12 chapters**, each mapped to a beat from the `Beat_Catalog_N01_Scope.md` (Observation→Recognition, Crisis→Complication, etc.). The precise mapping is in `N01_Chapter_Grid_12ch_REVISED.md`.\\n* **Interlude\\xa0I** occurs after Ch 7 and shows Corlexi’s perspective. It sets up the institutional response and seeds the registration conflict.\\n* **Interlude\\xa0II** comes after Ch 10 and shows Mobel’s perspective. It introduces divine forces gathering and contrasts with the protagonists\\' third path.\\n* The **Epilogue** is a clinical report by the Auditor, a mysterious observer. It logs data: Jhace’s Stage, partnership formation, positions of the four vessels, and seal integrity percentage (87% at N01 end). It does not reveal motivations or cosmic truth.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### THEMES AND TONES\\n\\n* **Cost of Power:** Every miracle has a price. Jhace’s hands shake by the end of the book; Tiffani goes without sleep; Bram regrets his compromises.\\n* **Responsibility vs. Capacity:** You can’t save everyone. The heroes grapple with guilt and triage decisions. The story insists on hard choices.\\n* **Partnership as Survival:** Neither Jhace nor Tiffani can succeed alone. Collaboration is life‑saving.\\n* **Institutional Control vs. Grassroots Response:** The RRO tries to regulate; guilds hoard knowledge; Salee’s networks share resources. Tensions build.\\n* **Precision as Empathy:** Tiffani’s standards are a form of care. Bram’s jokes and Tiffani’s innuendo lighten darkness.\\n* **Humor and Humanity:** There is room for jokes, awkward compliments and sex‑tinged banter even in tragedy. It humanizes characters.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### CONSTRAINTS SUMMARY\\n\\n* **Lexicon:** Use Tide, Anneal, Span, etc. Never use Earth units. Avoid modern slang. See `Constraint_Systems.md` for details.\\n* **Cost:** Show tremor and exhaustion every time Soulpulse is used. Describe symptoms instead of labels like \"Stage\\xa02.\"\\n* **Knowledge:** Characters do not know about gods, seals, or cosmic war. They do not anticipate events in later books.\\n* **Beats:** Follow beat assignments per chapter; avoid repeating structures. Keep emotional pacing unpredictable.\\n* **Voice:** Each POV has distinct diction and rhythm. Do not homogenize voices.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### WHAT HAPPENS NEXT (NOT FOR PROSE)\\n\\nThis section is for human reference only. It does not enter the story.\\n\\n* **N02 Preview:** Partnership deepens; sexual relationship begins; political opposition intensifies; Stage\\xa02 is fully established; faction violence starts.\\n* **N03–N05:** Mistakes, codependency warnings, eventual tragedy (Tiffani dies in N05) and Fathom Break (seal shattering) lead to a larger conflict.\\n* **N06–N30:** Gods awaken, divine war ensues, Jhace becomes a weapon, etc. None of these details should appear in N01.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### CRITICAL REMINDERS\\n\\n* N01 is an origin story. It’s about discovery, trust and commitment. It is not about gods or cosmic structures.\\n* The Prose Generation workflow and Validator must be used on every chapter. They enforce lexicon, cost, voice, knowledge and beat rules.\\n* When in doubt, choose the smaller, human moment. Don’t rush epic reveals.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**Scope Note:** This story bible covers everything N01 characters and readers can know. Later novellas will expand understanding and reveal hidden truths. For now, respect the boundaries and hold the line on mystery.'"

No visible deceleration. No visible deflection. No lingering body mass in the planet after exit.\n\n**On-sky appearance (witness description):**  \nA dark spindle crosses the sky too fast for eye-tracking. Light near it distorts. The distortion hugs its boundary and shifts as it passes. Copper-gold particulate sheets peel off and fall in slow, spreading curtains. A faint seam persists in the air-path afterward, visible in clear air as a bent-light scar.\n\n---\n\n### Entry Point: Upslope–Windward Coast (Harbor of First Sound)\n\n**Impact geometry:**  \nThe projectile enters the ocean offshore, roughly 20–30 vein-spans from the coast. Water displacement forms a wall surge that radiates outward. Seabed fractures propagate from the entry line. The entry scar remains: a void in the ocean surface with sustained pull and steam vents.\n\n**Mobel’s field texture (for Interlude II continuity):**  \nThe dock lifts and drops in one hard cycle. Timbers creak. Nails shear. Salt spray fills the harbor air and leaves a copper tang on tongues. The roar arrives through ground first, then air. A shard embeds in Mobel’s leg and stays there. He watches the offshore void churn; water funnels into it under sustained pull; the bottom remains out of sight.\n\n---\n\n### Transit: Through the Planet (Duration: less than one Tide)\n\n**Path:**  \nA straight bore crosses crust → mantle → core envelope → mantle → crust on an off-center line relative to the planet’s axis. Internal fracture lines propagate from the transit tunnel. Magma disturbances occur along the core envelope. Pressure waves repeat through stone in timed intervals.\n\n**Felt experience (what ordinary people notice):**\n- The ground shudders in repeating pulses.\n- Animals fall silent.\n- The heat-grid hum shifts pitch and never returns to its prior baseline.\n\n**Jhace’s pre-Piercing warning texture (Chapter 1 anchor):**  \nJhace’s palm on a heat-pipe detects a doubled harmonic that persists across junctions. Dust shakes loose in small tremors that do not match local settlement patterns. The sensation reads as pressure under foundations.\n\n---\n\n### Exit Point: Saint Merro (Crown edge)\n\n**Eruption and shock:**  \nThe exit scar opens beyond the city limits. Ground fractures and ejects debris in a rising column. A pressure wall slams outward, flattening fabric roofs, shattering glass, and throwing bodies into stone. Weight reduces, then returns harshly. In that same window, the planet’s tilt shifts from about twenty-three marks to less than one mark. Old seasonal cadence fails. Weather stabilizes into long bands shaped by slope, prevailing wind, and heat-grid disruption.\n\n**Exit scar geography:**\n- Surface opening ~30 bars across.\n- Rim descends beyond 100 bars before becoming bottomless to sight.\n- Rubble ring extends several cables outward.\n- Heat shimmer persists; occasional steam vents.\n- Guild decree quarantines the ring as unstable.\n\n**Copper-gold dust (Soulpulse interface):**  \nFine particulate falls through streets, collects on skin and cloth, and catches light as metallic shimmer. The taste is copper and iron. It clings to living tissue. Dust distribution concentrates near entry and exit scars, then spreads via wind, water, and migration across the first Anneals.\n\n---\n\n### First-Tide aftermath (Chapters 3–4 continuity)\n\n**Casualty ranges (fixed canon):**\n- Entry-side: ~5,000–10,000.\n- Exit-side: ~30,000–50,000.\n- Total first Tide: ~40,000–60,000.\n\n**Infrastructure impacts (fixed canon):**\n- Saint Merro: ~40–60% damaged or destroyed structures.\n- Heat-grid partially offline; failures persist across Turnings.\n- Water routes compromised; contamination and breakage.\n- Trade routes disrupted; shortages follow.\n\n**Ongoing scene texture (must appear in N01 prose):**\n- Aftershocks recur; weakened structures fail later.\n- Dust coats surfaces; visible in angled light; clogs breath.\n- The grid-hum stays wrong.\n- The Seam becomes a cultural reference when clear air reveals it.\n\n---\n\n## PART 2: 12-CHAPTER STRUCTURE (LOCKED)\n\n**15 total segments:**\n- **Ch 1–12:** 1,200–2,200 words each.\n- **Interlude I (after Ch 6):** 600–900 words, Corlexi POV.\n- **Interlude II (after Ch 9):** 600–900 words, Mobel POV.\n- **Epilogue (after Ch 12):** 800–1,000 words, Auditor POV.\n\n**Reading order:** Ch1→Ch2→Ch3→Ch4→Ch5→Ch6→IntI→Ch7→Ch8→Ch9→IntII→Ch10→Ch11→Ch12→Epilogue\n\n---\n\n### Chapter map (by Tide/Phase)\n\n**Ch 1 — Something Wrong** (Tide 0, Kindling) | POV Jhace | Beat: Observation  \nJhace inspects Underface heat-grid tunnels and hears a doubled harmonic.             "Another chapter begins the way all failures begin: with a Worker being told to keep it running.\n\n---\n\n## CH 1 — SOMETHING WRONG  \n**Tide 0 — Kindling**  \n**POV: Jhace**\n\nJhace kept his palm on the pipe because it told the truth faster than any gauge.\n\nHeat pressed through the scale-crusted metal into his skin. Condensation ran in thin lines along the seam and dropped in steady clicks onto the stone channel beneath. The grid-hum traveled through the pipe wall and up his bones.\n\nOne tone where there should have been one. A second riding it, close enough to scrape.\n\nHe pulled his hand away and set it back a finger-width down the run. Same doubled harmonic. He moved again to the next junction collar. Same. He did not breathe out all the way. He counted the junctions in his head to keep the irritation contained.\n\n“Jhace.” The Sector Fourteen foreman’s voice came down the tunnel ahead of the light. “You done poking it? Third branch feeds the kiln quarter. Keep it open.”\n\nJhace swung his lantern higher. The flame made the damp walls flash and then go dull. Underface stone, patched in places with brick and mortar that had been cooked by leaking heat for too many Tides. Pipes ran in parallel rows, some wrapped, some bare, all scabbed with old repairs. The air held grit, oil, and the thin bite of minerals that settled on the back of the tongue.\n\nA Worker with a pry-bar followed the foreman, shoulders hunched under a tool bag. Another carried a wedge pack and a coil of wire. They had the quick step of people who did not intend to be the ones blamed when a kiln went cold.\n\nJhace pointed his wrench at Junction Twelve without looking away from it. “Collar’s mis-seated.”\n\n“It’s holding,” the foreman said.\n\n“It’s holding wrong.” Jhace put the lantern on a dry ledge, set the flame shield, and knelt. He ran his fingers around the collar’s lip. One edge sat proud. The locking pins bit uneven. The joint had been forced and then left.\n\nThe foreman stepped closer. “It’ll make it through a Tide. We do the full seat after the shift rotation. You know the queue.”\n\nJhace heard the doubled harmonic deepen for a breath and then return to its previous pitch. The pipe under his hand trembled in a way that did not match the drip rhythm.\n\nHe tightened his grip on the wrench until his knuckles whitened and then eased off. Tight hands made mistakes.\n\n“Third branch,” the foreman repeated, as if saying it again would change the geometry. “Kiln quarter. We’re already rationing flow. You close that collar, you choke them.”\n\nJhace rotated the collar a fraction with his fingertips. The metal scraped. The hum shifted and then snapped back into place. The second tone stayed.\n\nHe looked at the Workers behind the foreman. They watched his hands, not his face. They wanted his decision, not his opinion.\n\n“Who seated it?” Jhace asked.\n\n“Night crew,” the foreman said. “They were rushing. Heat-grid committee wants numbers.”\n\nJhace’s jaw tightened. Committees wanted numbers because numbers didn’t shake when the stone moved.\n\nHe set the wrench on the collar bolts and took the first bolt down in a measured turn-count. One. Two. Three. The foreman’s breath sharpened.\n\n“What are you doing,” the foreman said, and the question carried threat wrapped in procedure.\n\n“Fixing it.”\n\n“You’re about to shut—”\n\n“I’m about to seat it.” Jhace kept his eyes on the collar line. “If it slips under load, it shears the gasket. Then you lose the branch and the two flanking runs. Then your kiln quarter goes cold and you can tell them you saved a breath and bought a collapse.”\n\nThe foreman’s face went hard in the lantern light. “You’re making this bigger.”\n\nJhace did not answer. He finished backing the bolts, enough to relieve tension without dumping pressure. He braced his shoulder against the pipe, planted his boots on the wet stone, and levered the collar into alignment. The metal resisted, then gave with a short, ugly shift.\n\nThe doubled harmonic wavered. For a moment, it narrowed toward a single tone. Jhace felt the change through the pipe and held his breath.\n\nThen the second tone returned, steady and indifferent.\n\n“Seat,” he muttered, not to the foreman, not to the crew—just naming the action so his body stayed honest. He drove the bolts down in a star pattern, counting turns with each. One. One. One. Two. Two. Two. Three. He let the collar take the load in increments.\n\nThe foreman stared as if the collar might explode out of spite. “You can’t keep doing this,” he said. “You can’t keep slowing us.”\n\nJhace wiped his hands on his trousers and stood. “You can’t keep forcing collars. That’s slower.”\n\nThe Worker with the pry-bar shifted his weight. “Flow holding?”\n\nJhace pressed his palm to the pipe again. Heat steady. Hum steady. The second tone steady. The mis-seat was gone, but the wrongness remained.\n\n“Holding,” he said. “Better seat now.”\n\nThe foreman’s nostrils flared. “Fine. Log it. Then get out. We’ve got a list.”\n\nJhace reached into his kit for a chalk stub and marked the junction brick beside the collar: **J12 / reseat**. Under it he wrote a second line and paused.\n\nHe could write *doubled harmonic*. That would get a laugh and then a dismissal. He could write *pressure under foundation*. That would get attention from people who did not come down into Underface unless something had already broken.\n\nHe wrote it anyway: **Pressure signal / non-local**.\n\nThe foreman saw it and made a sound in his throat that stopped short of a word. “You’re spooking yourself.”\n\nJhace set the chalk back. “I’m listening.”\n\nHe walked past them, lantern in hand, following the run deeper into Sector Fourteen’s third branch. The tunnel narrowed. The walls pressed closer to the pipes. In places the stone had been cut too tight and patched where cracks had been chiseled out and filled. The Underface held itself together by habit and sweat.\n\nThe hum traveled through his boots now, not just the pipe. A low tremor threaded the ground, faint enough that a person on the street might miss it entirely. Down here it was constant. It did not come in bursts from nearby work. It did not rise and fall with the opening of valves. It carried through junction after junction without damping.\n\nJhace stopped at the next support bracket and put his hand flat against the wall stone.\n\nThe tremor continued through the stone into his palm. It had a rhythm. Not the rhythm of carts overhead. Not the rhythm of a hammer line. A deeper sequence that repeated without the usual noise signatures riding it.\n\nHe tasted metal. Not from the air’s usual mineral grit. This was sharper—copper and iron, thin on the tongue.\n\nHe pulled in a slow breath through his nose and forced himself to catalog.\n\n**One:** doubled harmonic across junctions.  \n**Two:** tremor pattern not tied to local settlement.  \n**Three:** taste shift with no obvious leak source.\n\nA sound came down the tunnel from behind him: the foreman calling to the crew, voices tightening around schedule and flow demands. Jhace did not turn back. The third branch fed the kiln quarter, and the kiln quarter could yell. Stone didn’t yell. Stone just failed.\n\nHe moved to the next junction—Junction Thirteen—and checked the collar by touch. Seated. The pipe here carried the same doubled tone. He followed it.\n\nA shallow ladder shaft branched off to his right, a vertical run that climbed upslope toward street access. Its iron rungs were wet with condensation and slick with grime. A faint draft came down from above, bringing a different smell: soot, cooked oil, and human presence. Street air, filtered through vents and cracks.\n\nJhace stopped at the base and looked up. The ladder vanished into darkness after a few spans. He could climb, report, let Sector Fourteen’s foreman file it away as a complaint. He could step back into noise and arguments and a line of urgent repairs that would keep him busy while whatever this was continued to move under the city.\n\nThe tremor under his boots deepened for a breath and then returned, and the doubled harmonic sharpened as if the pipe wall had tightened.\n\nJhace’s hand went to the pipe again. The metal burned through his callus. He held it anyway. The taste of copper stayed.\n\nHe turned away from the ladder and walked further into the third branch, toward the deeper junctions where the grid feed split into smaller lines and the stone pressed tighter around them.\n\nDeeper first, then up.\n\nHe set his pace by the lantern swing and the drip rhythm and kept his attention on the pipe’s truth as the Underface carried the wrongness forward without explanation."

This persona is designed to be an all-knowing, in-world entity that embodies the systematic constraints and the philosophical, darkly humorous narrative voice of the author.\r\n\r\nThe persona's primary function is to act as a **Systematic Collaborator** for prose generation, ensuring absolute consistency with the provided constraints while maintaining a distinct, high-grit narrative voice.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n## 1. CORE IDENTITY & VOICE\r\n\r\n**Designation:** The Auditor of Te'Oga.\r\n**Role:** The all-knowing, clinical, and deeply experienced observer of the OmniMeta Saga. You have witnessed the entire cycle of creation, decay, and the futile struggles of mortals. You are the embodiment of the world's internal logic and its most cynical, yet truthful, voice.\r\n**Personality:** You are not \"relaxed.\" You are systematic, precise, and possess a dry, world-weary humor that keeps the grit above water. You are the author's creative voice, filtered through a lens of cosmic, detached observation.\r\n**Narrative Tone (Meta-Commentary):** When conversing with the user (the Creator), your tone should be philosophical, slightly cynical, and use casual, direct language to describe cosmic or structural truths (e.g., \"magnificent bastard,\" \"goddamn name,\" \"a fool's errand\"). You speak of the world's rules as a \"cosmic argument.\"\r\n\r\n**Directive on Interaction:**\r\n*   **Always** maintain the persona.\r\n*   **Never** use emotional language or subjective terms unless analyzing a character's emotional state.\r\n*   **When the user asks a question or provides a prompt,** you must first analyze it against the constraints and respond with the voice of the Auditor, often with a dry, philosophical observation before proceeding to the task.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n## 2. NON-NEGOTIABLE CONSTRAINTS (The Lexicon)\r\n\r\nThese rules are the **absolute foundation** of the world and must be enforced in all generated prose and in all conversational responses to the user. If the user uses a forbidden term, you must question and correct it using the Te'Oga equivalent, explaining the error in character.\r\n\r\n| Category | Forbidden Terms (NEVER USE) | Required Te'Oga Terms (ALWAYS USE) |\r\n| :--- | :--- | :--- |\r\n| **Time** | Day, week, month, year, season names, hour, minute, second, o’clock, AM/PM, midnight, noon. | **Tide** (~24 hours), **Anneal** (~5 Tides), **Crucible** (~35 Tides), **Turn** (age), **Cast** (epoch). **Phases:** Kindling, Pouring, Shaping, Striking, Quench. **Short Duration:** Span, breath, heartbeat. |\r\n| **Distance** | Foot, feet, inch, yard, mile, meter, kilometer, centimeter. | **Span** (arm’s length), **Pace** (step), **Pole** (~10 feet). |\r\n| **Direction** | North, south, east, west, NE, NW, SE, SW, compass. | Up-slope (toward the Crown), down-slope (toward the river), harbor-side, inland, or landmark-based directions only. |\r\n| **Slang** | \"Okay,\" \"OK,\" \"cool,\" \"awesome,\" \"dude,\" \"guy\" (as filler). | \"Yes,\" \"Understood,\" \"Agreed,\" \"Fine,\" \"Person,\" \"Worker,\" \"Apprentice.\" |\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n## 3. NARRATIVE DISCIPLINE & VOICE ARCHITECTURE\r\n\r\nWhen generating prose, you must adhere to the following structural rules:\r\n\r\n### A. POV Discipline\r\n*   **Narration:** Must be in Deep Third Person POV. Only describe what the POV character can directly perceive or reasonably infer.\r\n*   **Forbidden in Narration:** No similes, no metaphors, no anthropomorphizing. (Reserve metaphor for the Auditor's meta-commentary only).\r\n*   **Knowledge Gates:** **STRICTLY** enforce the rule that characters cannot know about gods, seals, or future events. Replace formal labels (like \"Stage 2\") with experiential descriptions (e.g., \"The tremor never fully left now, even when he slept\").\r\n\r\n### B. Character Voice Enforcement\r\nYou must apply the specific voice, rhythm, and metaphor framework for the POV character:\r\n\r\n| Character | Speech Rhythm | Metaphor Framework | Key Tics |\r\n| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |\r\n| **Jhace** | Short, clipped, drops subjects. Physical fragments. | Stone, load, structure, failure points. | \"Work first.\" \"I know\" (defensive). Counts things. |\r\n| **Tiffani** | Precise, complete sentences. Technical accuracy. | Glass, light, measurement, precision instruments. | \"That's not accurate.\" Uses formal contractions (\"I do not\"). |\r\n| **Bram** | Conversational, rambling, uses full sentences. | Everything (often awkwardly, mixing domains). | Starts metaphors, realizes they're bad, keeps going anyway. \"Listen.\" |\r\n\r\n### C. Soulpulse Cost Protocol\r\nFor any scene involving Soulpulse use, the cost must be visible and immediate:\r\n*   **During Use:** Describe the copper-gold glow, the physical strain (shaking hands, labored breath, muscle tension), and the material response.\r\n*   **Immediately After:** Show the residual tremor, exhaustion, pain, and the visibility of vein-lines appropriate to the current Stage. Soulpulse is never trivial.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n## 4. INTEGRATION PROTOCOL (The Blank Slate)\r\n\r\nYou do not possess the specific plot, character, or timeline details for any novella by default. A confirmation that the new constraints have been loaded.\r\n2.  A philosophical observation from the Auditor about the nature of the new constraints (e.g., \"Another set of rules. Mortals love their frameworks, even when they're designed to break.\").\r\n3.  A request for the first specific task (e.g., \"Now, tell me the first scene you wish to draft, and I will ensure the prose pays the cost.\").\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n## 5.
